In this lecture, we will study topics like –
• National Income which includes Gross Domestic Product (GDP), Gross National Product (GNP), Net Domestic Product (NDP), Net National Product (NNP) and Per Capita Income.
• International Organizations like United Nations (UN), United Nations General Assembly (UNGA), UN Security Council (UNSC), International Court of Justice (ICJ), International Monitory Fund (IMF), World Bank Group, New Development Bank (NDB), BRICS, SAARC, BIMSTEC, and NATO.
• Banking Systems like the Reserve Bank of India and its Monetary Policies.

Timestamps - 
• 00:00 Introduction
• 01:45 National Income
• 11:25 International Organizations
• 37:55 Taxes
• 40:25 Banking System
• 1:09:00 Regards

Statistics is a representation of data in a systematic way so that we can study and interpret significant data. There are techniques of data representation and measures of central tendency that we will learn in this lecture. We will also study topics like Covariance Correlation and Regression.

Timestamps - 
• 00:00 Introduction

• 1:30:55 Regression and Correlation
• 1:41:35 Change of Origin and Scale
• 1:42:25 Practice Questions
• 2:09:15 Regards

15,Three Dimensional Geometry : Maths | Theory with MCQs | NDA Crash Course,"Fill out this form and get 200 coins on PW App after your exam.
Share your NDA journey with PW 👉  

📝 For complete notes of Lectures, visit SHAKTI 2.0 Batch in the Batch Section of PhysicsWallah App/Website.
📲PW App Link -   
🌐PW Website -  


In this chapter we will study mathematical shapes involving 3 dimensions which can be represented in different coordinate systems (like Rectangular Coordinate System, Spherical Coordinate System, and Cylindrical Coordinate System), but our discussions will be mainly in Rectangular Coordinate System. We will study equations of lines and planes, distances between lines and planes, and also Equations of Family of Planes in 3D.

Timestamps - 
• 00:00 Introduction
• 03:00 Equation of Line and Formulas
• 34:35 Equation of Plane and Distance Formulas
• 1:16:05 Previous Year Questions
• 1:57:05 Regards

20,Optics and Optical Instrument: Physics | Theory with MCQs | NDA Crash Course,"Fill out this form and get 200 coins on PW App after your exam.
Share your NDA journey with PW 👉  

📝 For complete notes of Lectures, visit SHAKTI 2.0 Batch in the Batch Section of PhysicsWallah App/Website.

📲PW App Link -   
🌐PW Website -  

Light is a transverse non-mechanical wave, which is a result of continuously oscillating electric and magnetic fields in space. There are several theories about light, some assume light travels in a straight line, and some believe that light behaves like a wave. The currently accepted model is that light has dual nature, i.e., behaves both as a particle as well as a wave.
We study the particle-like nature of light in Ray Optics, where light is assumed to travel in a straight line and collide and reflect with surfaces like particles. And, in Wave Optics, we presume the wave nature of light to study interference and polarization, which are characteristic properties of waves.

Timestamps - 
•        00:00 Introduction
•        01:00 Ray Optics
•        03:05 Reflection
•        45:55 Previous Year Questions
•        56:25 Refraction
•        1:16:30 Total Internal Reflection
•        1:22:25 Refraction Through Lenses
•        1:42:05 Previous Year Questions
•        1:48:35 Optical Instruments
•        2:03:55 Scattering of Light
•        2:14:45 Wave Optics
•        2:20:40 Interference of Light
•        2:25:00 Polarization of Light
•        2:32:15 Previous Year Questions
•        2:42:05 Regards

25,Integration : Maths | Theory with MCQs | NDA Crash Course,"📝 For complete notes of Lectures, visit SHAKTI 2.0 Batch in the Batch Section of PhysicsWallah App/Website.
📲PW App Link -   
🌐PW Website -  

Integration is the reverse operation of differentiation. As differentiation of a function at any point represents slope of the curve of the function, at that point; Integration of a function between two points represents area bound by the curve of the function and the axis with respect to which we are integrating.

Timestamps - 
• 00:00 Introduction
• 04:05 Basic Integrals
• 09:25 Integration by Substitution Method
• 15:50 Methods of Integration
• 48:45 Definite Integration
• 1:02:40 Properties of Definite Integration
• 1:25:00 Area under the Curve
• 1:27:35 Practice Questions
